## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task belongs to chemical kinetics, specifically modeling the time evolution of a reactant concentration A through its differential rate equation dA/dt. The relationship typically follows rate laws where the reaction rate depends on powers of concentration and possibly time-dependent factors like catalyst deactivation or temperature ramps.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- First-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular reactant decay)
- Second-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular collision process)
- Fractional-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (complex or chain reaction mechanisms)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product accelerates its own formation)
- Reversible first-order reaction: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 (approach to chemical equilibrium)
- Catalyst deactivation kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (time-dependent rate constant due to catalyst poisoning)
- Fractal/diffusion-limited kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A (changing transport limitations over time)
- Elovich-type surface reaction: dA_dt = c0 * exp(-c1 * A) (decreasing surface reactivity with coverage)
- Power-law time modulation: dA_dt = -c0 * A * t**c1 (flow reactor residence time or temperature programming effects)
- Dual-pathway parallel decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous first and second order consumption routes)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear negative dependence on concentration → First-order unimolecular decay with constant half-life
- Quadratic or higher power dependence on concentration → Bimolecular/termolecular collision dominance
- Bilinear form A*(C - A) → Autocatalytic behavior producing sigmoidal concentration-time profiles
- Time-modulated rate coefficient (t**c or exp(-c*t)) → Catalyst deactivation, thermal ramps, or diffusion control
- Additive constant offset in rate expression → Reversible reactions approaching thermodynamic equilibrium
- Exponential dependence of rate on concentration (exp(-c*A)) → Heterogeneous surface deactivation or Elovich kinetics
- Fractional power-law scaling with time multiplied by concentration → Fractal kinetics or evolving reaction dimensionality
- Rate independent of concentration (constant negative value) → Zero-order regime under catalyst saturation or surface limitation

The user wants to identify which of the 62 candidates mathematically equate to the Ground Truth (GT).

**Ground Truth (GT):**
Equation: `-c0*A + c1*_t*sin(log(A + c2))`
Numerical values:
c0 = 0.15727681835797813
c1 = 0.15727681835797813
c2 = 1.0
_t = 3.122751145472426
So GT = `-0.15727681835797813 * A + 0.49113636468363491 * sin(log(A + 1))`
Wait, `c1 * _t` = `0.15727681835797813 * 3.122751145472426` ≈ `0.4911363646836349`.
So GT is of the form: `C1 * A + C2 * sin(log(A + 1))`
where `C1 = -0.15727681835797813` and `C2 = 0.49113636468363491`.
Actually, the GT symbolic expression is `-c0*A + c1*_t*sin(log(A + c2))`.
Let's denote `k1 = -c0`, `k2 = c1*_t`, `k3 = c2`.
So GT = `k1 * A + k2 * sin(log(A + k3))`.
With `k3 = 1`.
So GT = `k1 * A + k2 * sin(log(A + 1))`.

We need to check each candidate to see if it can be simplified to `C_A * A + C_S * sin(log(A + 1))` by adjusting its free constants.
Note: Candidates have their own constants `c0, c1, ...` which are free. I will rename them to avoid confusion with GT constants, or just treat them as free parameters.

Let's analyze the candidates one by one.

**Candidate 1:**

This is a rational function with exponentials. It cannot match `A + sin(log(A+1))`.
Verdict: NO MATCH.

`A*c0 + c1 + c2*log(A*c3 + 1) + c4*sin(c5*log(A*c6 + 1) + c7)`
This has `log` and `sin(log(...))`. The GT has `sin(log(A+1))`.
Can `c2*log(A*c3 + 1)` be zero? Yes, set `c2=0`.
Can `c4*sin(c5*log(A*c6 + 1) + c7)` match `k2 * sin(log(A+1))`?
Yes, set `c6=1`, `c5=1`, `c7=0`, `c4=k2`.
Can `A*c0 + c1` match `k1 * A`? Yes, set `c0=k1`, `c1=0`.
So Candidate 2 can match exactly.
Wait, let's check carefully: `A*c0 + c1 + c2*log(A*c3 + 1) + c4*sin(c5*log(A*c6 + 1) + c7)`
Set `c0 = k1`, `c1 = 0`, `c2 = 0`, `c3 = 0` (or anything), `c4 = k2`, `c5 = 1`, `c6 = 1`, `c7 = 0`.

**Candidate 3:**
`A*c0/(c1 + 1/sqrt(A)) + A*(A*c2 + c3)/(A*c4 + 1) + c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7 + 1) + c8)`
The first two terms are rational functions of A and sqrt(A). They cannot simplify to a linear term `k1*A` exactly for all A, unless coefficients are zero.
If `c0=0`, first term is 0.
Second term: `A*(A*c2 + c3)/(A*c4 + 1)`. To be linear `k1*A`, we need `(A*c2 + c3)/(A*c4 + 1) = k1`. This implies `c2 = k1*c4` and `c3 = k1`. But then it's `k1*A` exactly. Wait, `(A*k1*c4 + k1)/(A*c4 + 1) = k1*(A*c4+1)/(A*c4+1) = k1`. So yes, it can be `k1*A`.

So yes, Candidate 3 can match.
Let's double check. `A*(A*c2 + c3)/(A*c4 + 1)`. If `c2 = k1*c4` and `c3 = k1`, then it's `k1*A`.

### Ground Truth Analysis
The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`-c0*A + c1*_t*sin(log(A + c2))`
With the given numerical constants (`c0≈0.157`, `c1≈0.157`, `c2=1.0`, `_t≈3.123`), this simplifies to a concrete function of the form:
`GT(A) = k1 * A + k2 * sin(log(A + 1))`
where `k1 = -0.1572768...` and `k2 = 0.4911363...`.
Any candidate must be algebraically reducible to exactly `C_A * A + C_S * sin(log(A + 1))` by assigning appropriate values to its free constants. Basis functions like `exp`, `log`, `cos`, `sqrt`, or linear arguments inside `sin` cannot match the required `A` and `sin(log(A+1))` terms due to linear independence.

### Candidate Analysis

**Candidate 2:** `A*c0 + c1 + c2*log(A*c3 + 1) + c4*sin(c5*log(A*c6 + 1) + c7)`. Set `c2=0`, `c1=0`, `c0=k1`, `c4=k2`, `c5=1`, `c6=1`, `c7=0`. Reduces exactly to `k1*A + k2*sin(log(A+1))`. `[MATCH]`
**Candidate 3:** `A*c0/(c1 + 1/sqrt(A)) + A*(A*c2 + c3)/(A*c4 + 1) + c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7 + 1) + c8)`. Set `c0=0` (eliminates first term). Set `c4=1, c2=k1, c3=k1` (second term becomes `k1*A`). Set `c5=k2, c6=1, c7=1, c8=0` (third term matches). `[MATCH]`

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK25)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A + c1*_t*sin(log(A + c2))
Candidates evaluated: 62
Matched candidate IDs: [2, 3, 13, 14, 15]
Matched candidates: ["A*c0 + c1 + c2*log(A*c3 + 1) + c4*sin(c5*log(A*c6 + 1) + c7)", "A*c0/(c1 + 1/sqrt(A)) + A*(A*c2 + c3)/(A*c4 + 1) + c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7 + 1) + c8)", "(A**2*c0 + A*c1 + c2*(A + c3)*sin(log(A + 1)))/(A + c3)", "A*c0 + A + c1*sin(log(A + 1))", "A*c0 + c1*sin(log(A + 1))"]

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: -0.15727681835797813*A + 0.49113636468363491*sin(log(A + 1))**

This is a function of A only (not t), with two terms: a linear term in A and a sin(log(A+1)) term.

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. I'll focus on identifying which candidates can reduce to the form `c*A + d*sin(log(A+1))`.

**Key observations about GT:**
- It's a function of A only (no t dependence)
- It contains exactly two basis functions: A and sin(log(A+1))
- No exponential terms, no polynomial terms beyond linear, no sqrt, no A^(1/3)

Let me go through candidates:

**Candidate 1:** Contains exp(A*c7) - exponential in A cannot be zeroed without losing other terms in the structure. Let me check: expanding gives `c0 + (c4 + c2*A*c5 + c2*c6*exp(A*c7) + c2*c8 + A*c5 + c6*exp(A*c7) + c8*... ` This has exp terms that can't match sin(log(A+1)). 
Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** `A*c0 + c1 + c2*log(A*c3 + 1) + c4*sin(c5*log(A*c6 + 1) + c7)`
Set c1=0, c2=0, then: `A*c0 + c4*sin(c5*log(A*c6+1) + c7)`. With c5=1, c6=1, c7=0: `A*c0 + c4*sin(log(A+1))`. This matches GT!
Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** Contains `1/sqrt(A)` and other rational terms plus `c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7+1)+c8)`. Setting c0=0 eliminates the sqrt term. Then `A*(A*c2+c3)/(A*c4+1) + c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7+1)+c8)`. The rational part `A*(A*c2+c3)/(A*c4+1)` - for this to be linear in A, we need c2=0 giving `A*c3/(A*c4+1)`. This is not linear unless c4=0, giving `A*c3`. With c4=0, c2=0: `A*c3 + c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7+1)+c8)`. Set c6=1, c7=1, c8=0. This matches!
Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 4:** `A^(1/3)*c0 + c0*c1/A + A*c2 + c3 + c4*log(A*c5+1) + c4*c1*log(A*c5+1)/A + c6/A`. Contains A^(1/3) and log terms, no sin(log). Cannot match.
Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 5:** Expanding: simplifies to same form as Candidate 4 structure with A^(1/3) and log terms. No sin(log).
Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 6:** Contains exp(A*c8). Let me check if exp can be zeroed. Expanding: `c0 + c4*(A+c5)/(A+c3) + c6/((A+c3)*(A*c1+c2)) + c7*exp(A*c8) + c9`. Setting c7=0, c6=0: `c0 + c4*(A+c5)/(A+c3) + c9`. This is rational, no sin(log). Cannot match.
Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 7:** Contains log(A*c8+1) terms. Expanding: `c1 + c2/(A+c0) + (A*c3+c4)*[A^2*c5+A*c6+c7*(A+c0)*log(A*c8+1)+c9]/((A+c0)*(A*c3+c4))`. This has log but no sin(log).
Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 8:** Contains log(c5*exp(A*c6)+1). Note: log(c5*exp(A*c6)+1) is a softplus-like function, not sin(log). Cannot produce sin(log(A+1)).
Candidate 8 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 9:** Contains A^c6 term. Unless c6 is set to make it linear, but also no sin(log).
Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 10:** Contains log(A*c7+1) but no sin(log).
Candidate 10 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 11:** Contains log(c5*exp(A*c6)+1), no sin(log).
Candidate 11 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 12:** Contains exp(A*c8), no sin(log).
Candidate 12 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 13:** `(A^2*c0 + A*c1 + c2*(A+c3)*sin(log(A+1)))/(A+c3)`. Expanding: `(A^2*c0+A*c1)/(A+c3) + c2*sin(log(A+1))`. For the rational part to be linear: `A^2*c0+A*c1 = (A+c3)*(αA) = αA^2+αc3*A`. So c0=α, c1=α*c3. Then result: `αA + c2*sin(log(A+1))`. This matches!
Candidate 13 verdict: [MATCH]
